{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-23 23:59:05","updatedTime":"2020-08-23 23:59:05","title":"How To Help Your Clients Get More Backlinks Through Design","link":"https://www.smashingmagazine.com/2020/08/clients-backlinks-design/","description":"\n          <html>\n            <head>\n              <meta charset=\"utf-8\">\n              <link rel=\"canonical\" href=\"https://www.smashingmagazine.com/2020/08/clients-backlinks-design/\" />\n              <title>How To Help Your Clients Get More Backlinks Through Design</title>\n            </head>\n            <body>\n              <article>\n                <header>\n                  <h1>How To Help Your Clients Get More Backlinks Through Design</h1>\n                  \n                    \n                    <address>Suzanne Scacca</address>\n                  \n                  <time datetime=\"2020-08-21T10:30:00&#43;00:00\" class=\"op-published\">2020-08-21T10:30:00+00:00</time>\n                  <time datetime=\"2020-08-21T10:30:00&#43;00:00\" class=\"op-modified\">2020-08-23T15:35:52+00:00</time>\n                </header>\n                \n\n<p>There are certain truths when it comes to what helps a website rank in search. Google wants to see:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>Mobile-first design</li>\n<li>Fast page speeds</li>\n<li>Top-notch security</li>\n<li>User-friendly navigation</li>\n<li>Trustworthiness and expertise</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>… among other things. It also wants to see high-authority websites link back to your website.</p>\n\n<p>And if your clients aren’t obsessed with getting backlinks right now, just wait and see. They’re highly coveted and some businesses will go to great lengths to get them.</p>\n\n<p>Obviously, the quality of the content has to be there if it’s going to be share-worthy. However, the way a page looks can also make or break whether someone decides to share a link to it.</p>\n\n<p>You might not think this is something you can help with as a web designer, but you definitely can. And this post will provide you with a number of tips on how to contribute to this great quest for backlinks.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"how-to-design-sites-that-high-authority-sources-want-to-link-to\">How To Design Sites That High-Authority Sources Want To Link To</h3>\n\n<p>The quality of a backlinked page can reflect on the quality and reputation of the linking website, so authoritative sites have to be incredibly choosy about who they give backlinks to.</p>\n\n<p>The content needs to be reputable and valuable. That’s non-negotiable. But the design has to be top-of-the-line, too.</p>\n\n<p>Let’s take a look at some ways in which you can help your clients’ websites be seen as trustworthy sources worth linking to.</p>\n\n\n  <div data-component=\"FeaturePanel\" data-audience=\"non-subscriber\" data-remove=\"true\" class=\"feature-panel-container hidden\"></div>\n\n\n<h4 id=\"tip-1-visualize-data-whenever-possible\">Tip #1: Visualize Data Whenever Possible</h4>\n\n<p>In my line of work, one of the most common reasons I link to other websites is to cite data that they discovered or own. I do this to strengthen my points as well as to lend credibility to the arguments I’m making.</p>\n\n<p>That said, there usually isn’t just one organization doing research on the topics I’m interested in, which means I need to figure out which site is worth linking to. And that often comes down to how well they’ve visually depicted the data.</p>\n\n<p>To be clear, I’m not just referring to statistical data. This also pertains to things like breakdowns of processes. Like if I’m researching how various companies handle a given task and a website has a great visual depiction of their workflow, I may be more inclined to link to that page since it’s more valuable.</p>\n\n<p>Let me show you an example.</p>\n\n<p>Let’s say I’m writing an article about why people uninstall mobile apps. I don’t just want to cite a random list of what I think are the reasons for something like this. I know that the evidence exists, so I go searching for sources that can back me up.</p>\n\n<p>In my research on the subject, I find two credible sources that present similar sets of findings. This article appeared on <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/ciocentral/2013/11/21/why-people-uninstall-apps/#104d78384be4\">Forbes</a>:</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/987241e4-0c4a-41bd-88a7-1ba94a48b1c7/forbes-research-article-design.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/987241e4-0c4a-41bd-88a7-1ba94a48b1c7/forbes-research-article-design.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/987241e4-0c4a-41bd-88a7-1ba94a48b1c7/forbes-research-article-design.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/987241e4-0c4a-41bd-88a7-1ba94a48b1c7/forbes-research-article-design.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/987241e4-0c4a-41bd-88a7-1ba94a48b1c7/forbes-research-article-design.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/987241e4-0c4a-41bd-88a7-1ba94a48b1c7/forbes-research-article-design.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/987241e4-0c4a-41bd-88a7-1ba94a48b1c7/forbes-research-article-design.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Forbes article - ‘Why People Uninstall Apps’ - long walls of text and distracting ads\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      A Forbes article explains ‘Why People Uninstall Apps’. (Source: <a href='https://www.forbes.com/sites/ciocentral/2013/11/21/why-people-uninstall-apps/#104d78384be4'>Forbes</a>) (<a \n</figure>\n\n<p>And this blog post and infographic was published by <a href=\"https://clevertap.com/blog/uninstall-apps/\">CleverTap</a>:</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/41695563-d56c-42b4-a979-c43d432ceaaf/clevertap-article-infographic.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/41695563-d56c-42b4-a979-c43d432ceaaf/clevertap-article-infographic.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"CleverTap article and infographic - data presented visually and breaks down top reasons people uninstall apps\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      A CleverTap article and infographic explain ‘Why Users Uninstall App’. (Hint: It’s because 28% feel spammed.) (Source: <a href='https://clevertap.com/blog/uninstall-apps/'>CleverTap</a>) (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/41695563-d56c-42b4-a979-c43d432ceaaf/clevertap-article-infographic.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>Let’s say that the two surveys both have a large pool of respondents and the research was done recently. In that case, I’d turn my attention to the way in which the findings are presented.</p>\n\n<p>There are a number of reasons why I’d choose CleverTap over Forbes any day.</p>\n\n<p>For one, CleverTap translated its findings into a user-friendly format. We’ve known for years that infographics get more engagement and shares than plain text content. Sharing and linking are two different kinds of engagement, but we usually do them for the same reason:</p>\n\n<p><strong>We trust the source or find some value in the content and want others to discover it as well.</strong></p>\n\n<p>So, because CleverTap presented this beautiful breakdown of its findings, it’s enabled me to more quickly and effectively identify the facts I’m looking for, more so than the run-on paragraphs on the Forbes site. With Forbes’ presentation of the data, I’d basically have to copy-and-paste the content into my own document and do some formatting of my own to try and figure out what’s going on.</p>\n\n<blockquote class=\"pull-quote\">\n  <p>\n    <a class=\"pull-quote__link\" aria-label=\"Share on Twitter\" href=\"http://twitter.com/share?text=No%20one%20should%20have%20to%20work%20for%20their%20data,%20just%20like%20no%20one%20should%20have%20to%20work%20to%20get%20through%20a%20website.%0a&url=https://smashingmagazine.com%2f2020%2f08%2fclients-backlinks-design%2f\">\n      No one should have to work for their data, just like no one should have to work to get through a website.\n\n    </a>\n  </p>\n  <div class=\"pull-quote__quotation\">\n    <div class=\"pull-quote__bg\">\n      <span class=\"pull-quote__symbol\">“</span></div>\n  </div>\n</blockquote>\n\n<p>So, that’s reason number one. CleverTap shows extra care and consideration for the data that’s being presented as well as an understanding of the audience who needs to read it.</p>\n\n<p>Reason number two is that Forbes’s page is littered with ads. When one disappears, another two appear in its place. It’s distracting and I don’t believe in sending people to a website that so blatantly prioritizes its profits over its content. Again, linked-to websites can have an impact on the linking website’s reputation, so this is something to consider when you design your own.</p>\n\n<p>The last reason I’d link to CleverTap’s page over Forbes’ is because <a href=\"https://www.smashingmagazine.com/2020/05/data-visualization-mobile-web-experience/\">visually designed data</a> saves me the trouble of having to create graphics on my own. It’s not like I can’t cite the data as is, but why should I? I know that it’s easier for my readers to find key data points and understand them when I call them out visually.</p>\n\n<p>Plus, I’m already giving the linked website credit for their work, so I am more than happy to provide a companion branded image. It lends even more credibility to my source.</p>\n\n<div class=\"sponsors__lead-place\"></div>\n\n\n\n\n<h4 id=\"tip-2-make-lengthy-pages-easier-to-scan\">Tip #2: Make Lengthy Pages Easier To Scan</h4>\n\n<p>I have clients who constantly come to me and say, “I need you to write a 2,000-word article so I can rank #1 on Google.”</p>\n\n<p>This is one of those SEO myths that’s part fact and part fiction. Here’s why:</p>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://twitter.com/JohnMu\">Google’s John Mueller</a> is often asked on Twitter to confirm various assumptions we have about SEO (since Google itself is so tight-lipped about it). And that’s when we get useful gems like this:</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/42dae39a-6901-47bb-a07e-e313ef336547/google-john-mueller-on-page-length.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/42dae39a-6901-47bb-a07e-e313ef336547/google-john-mueller-on-page-length.png Mueller (@JohnMu) responds to a question on Twitter about how word count correlates with page rank\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      John Mueller (@JohnMu) responds to a question on Twitter about how word count correlates with page rank. (Source: <a href='https://twitter.com/JohnMu'>John Mueller on Twitter</a>) (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/42dae39a-6901-47bb-a07e-e313ef336547/google-john-mueller-on-page-length.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>That’s what I tell my clients, but without the snark obviously. It’s not about hitting a target number of words that will magically make a web page rank. All you need to do is match the search intent and then unpack the topic as fully as needed.</p>\n\n<p>That said, there is <a href=\"https://backlinko.com/content-study\">data from Backlinko</a> that confirms that longer pages do rank higher in search…</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/54a765de-d380-4158-8ceb-40143ce810da/backlinko-long-form-content-links.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/54a765de-d380-4158-8ceb-40143ce810da/backlinko-long-form-content-links.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/54a765de-d380-4158-8ceb-40143ce810da/backlinko-long-form-content-links.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/54a765de-d380-4158-8ceb-40143ce810da/backlinko-long-form-content-links.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Backlinko data: long-form content generates more backlinks than short blog posts\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Backlinko shows the correlation between number of words on a web page and how many backlinks it gets. (Source: <a href='https://backlinko.com/content-study'>Backlinko</a>) (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/54a765de-d380-4158-8ceb-40143ce810da/backlinko-long-form-content-links.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>But it’s not the sheer volume of words that lends to a lengthy web page’s rank. It’s because longer content tends to be more authoritative which makes it more link-worthy.</p>\n\n<p>Interesting, right?</p>\n\n<p>So, knowing this, you should do everything in your power to make a lengthy piece of content (any linkable page, really &#8212; including informational pages and the home page) super easy to scan, read and link to. Because even the most engaged reader is apt to miss important details or give up part of the way through if you don’t design the page the right way.</p>\n\n<p>For the purposes of this example, I’m going to show you two examples of long blog posts that are top-ranked for “how to price a saas product”.</p>\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.profitwell.com/blog/saas-pricing\">ProfitWell</a> handles it well enough and has 93 external followed links to show for it, according to <a href=\"https://moz.com/products/pro/seo-toolbar\">MozBar</a>. These are backlinks that pass SEO value onto Google, which is how a website ranks higher thanks to its backlink profile.</p>\n\n<p>All I probably need to do is show you what the above-the-fold looks like to demonstrate why this article hasn’t been linked to nearly as much as one of its competitors. Here it is:</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/e5cf21d9-1604-4270-994c-8c6169e31ea3/profitwell-saas-pricing-blog-post.png\">\n    \n ProfitWell article about pricing SaaS products\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      ProfitWell unpacks ‘SaaS pricing models, strategies and examples of success’. (Source: <a href='https://www.profitwell.com/blog/saas-pricing'>ProfitWell</a>) (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/e5cf21d9-1604-4270-994c-8c6169e31ea3/profitwell-saas-pricing-blog-post.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>In terms of overall design, ProfitWell has a great website. It’s even done a fantastic job laying out the post so it’s easy to scan through and read.</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/bc401368-0ced-49b3-a346-b1cbb5fc1234/profitwell-blog-post-with-graphics.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/bc401368-0ced-49b3-a346-b1cbb5fc1234/profitwell-blog-post-with-graphics.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/bc401368-0ced-49b3-a346-b1cbb5fc1234/profitwell-blog-post-with-graphics.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/bc401368-0ced-49b3-a346-b1cbb5fc1234/profitwell-blog-post-with-graphics.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/bc401368-0ced-49b3-a346-b1cbb5fc1234/profitwell-blog-post-with-graphics.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/bc401368-0ced-49b3-a346-b1cbb5fc1234/profitwell-blog-post-with-graphics.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/bc401368-0ced-49b3-a346-b1cbb5fc1234/profitwell-blog-post-with-graphics.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"ProfitWell blog post design and layout - header tags, bolding, hyperlinks, graphics and more\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      The ProfitWell blog post is designed to make reading and scanning easy. (Source: <a href='https://www.profitwell.com/blog/saas-pricing'>ProfitWell</a>) (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/bc401368-0ced-49b3-a346-b1cbb5fc1234/profitwell-blog-post-with-graphics.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>In just this screenshot alone you can see how effectively the designer has worked their magic on the page, including text enhancements like:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>Header tags,</li>\n<li>Bolded and highlighted hyperlinks,</li>\n<li>Data visualizations,</li>\n<li>Short sentence and paragraph structures,</li>\n<li>Bulleted and numbered lists.</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>However, it has a number of things working against it, which is what I believe has cost it backlinks.</p>\n\n<p>One is the overwhelming amount of distractions: the cumbersome sidebar, the sticky social share bar, the chat widget that needs to be dismissed and a lead gen pop-up that adheres to the bottom-left corner at times. Secondly, this is a long article. If people want to read it in full &#8212; especially on mobile &#8212; it’s going to take a lot of scrolling to get all the way through it.</p>\n\n<p>Now let me show you how <a href=\"https://www.cobloom.com/blog/saas-pricing-models#\">Cobloom</a>’s page design is likely why <strong>it has 159 external followed links.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/f24a6b17-152d-419d-9a49-b8778ad47d12/cobloom-saas-pricing-article.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/f24a6b17-152d-419d-9a49-b8778ad47d12/cobloom-saas-pricing-article.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/f24a6b17-152d-419d-9a49-b8778ad47d12/cobloom-saas-pricing-article.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"A Cobloom article on how to price SaaS products\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Cobloom’s ‘ultimate guide to SaaS pricing models, strategies & psychological hacks’. (Source: <a href='https://www.cobloom.com/blog/saas-pricing-models#'>Cobloom</a>) (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/f24a6b17-152d-419d-9a49-b8778ad47d12/cobloom-saas-pricing-article.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>This looks fantastic, right? There are three sticky elements always present:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>The sticky table of contents on the left,</li>\n<li>The chat widget which is part of the ToC bar,</li>\n<li>The social share widget.</li>\n</ul>\n\n<p>But the sticky parts of the page never compromise the content:</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca184adb-f9b8-4205-9f09-023ac493bc95/cobloom-blog-post-design.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca184adb-f9b8-4205-9f09-023ac493bc95/cobloom-blog-post-design.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca184adb-f9b8-4205-9f09-023ac493bc95/cobloom-blog-post-design.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca184adb-f9b8-4205-9f09-023ac493bc95/cobloom-blog-post-design.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca184adb-f9b8-4205-9f09-023ac493bc95/cobloom-blog-post-design.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca184adb-f9b8-4205-9f09-023ac493bc95/cobloom-blog-post-design.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca184adb-f9b8-4205-9f09-023ac493bc95/cobloom-blog-post-design.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Cobloom blog post design: sticky table of contents, sticky social share icons, sticky chat widget and well-designed content\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Cobloom’s blog post design and sticky elements make it easy for readers to digest the content. (Source: <a href='https://www.cobloom.com/blog/saas-pricing-models#'>Cobloom</a>) (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca184adb-f9b8-4205-9f09-023ac493bc95/cobloom-blog-post-design.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>In fact, the table of contents on the left makes the page easier to read (among other design choices that have been made). Readers can click on the section that they’re interested in without having to bother with scrolling down the page.</p>\n\n<p>The only thing I’d say this page falls short on is the mobile experience. The table of contents isn’t present and the page feels a little wobbly, as if the horizontal dimensions weren’t properly sized. So, in terms of this being a link-worthy page on mobile, I’d say it’s not when compared to ProfitWell’s super mobile-friendly post.</p>\n\n<p>But that’s a good lesson for you to take away from this. <a href=\"https://www.smashingmagazine.com/2020/01/mobile-pwa-sticky-bars-elements/\">Use your sticky elements on mobile wisely.</a> Rather than disrupt a post with a chat widget or a lead gen promotional bar, place the table of contents beneath it and let it serve as a secondary “navigation” for lengthier pages.</p>\n\n<div class=\"sponsors__lead-place\"></div>\n\n\n\n\n<h4 id=\"tip-3-design-each-page-s-metadata\">Tip #3: “Design” Each Page’s Metadata</h4>\n\n<p>As a writer, I spend a lot of time looking for the right links to place within my content. Which means a good chunk of my day is spent on Google, social media and Feedly trying to hunt down the perfect sources.</p>\n\n<p>Can you guess how I narrow down my options to ensure that I always share or link to the best content for my website visitors or social connections? I use the page’s metadata to help me decide.</p>\n\n<p>I’m not the only one who cares about the external “image” of a web page either. There’s <a href=\"https://buzzsumo.com/blog/how-to-massively-boost-your-blog-traffic-with-these-5-awesome-image-stats/\">plenty of research</a> that points to attractive social media content getting more shares than those that aren’t.</p>\n\n<p>So, in addition to designing pages to look more trustworthy and user-friendly, I’d suggest designing your metadata to make it look more carefully groomed. If you’ve taken the time to create a buttoned-up micro-image of the page, people looking for sources for their authoritative websites are more likely to give yours a closer look.</p>\n\n<p>As such, there are a couple things I’d recommend you do to increase the likelihood that this happens:</p>\n\n<p>The first thing is to ensure that the page’s metadata appears complete in search.</p>\n\n<p>For instance, here’s what comes up when I search <a href=\"https://www.google.com/\">Google</a> for “the most trusted brands in the world”:</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/e9176f63-71d8-4c5c-bb59-ff086506cda5/google-search-most-trusted-brands.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/e9176f63-71d8-4c5c-bb59-ff086506cda5/google-search-most-trusted-brands.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/e9176f63-71d8-4c5c-bb59-ff086506cda5/google-search-most-trusted-brands.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/e9176f63-71d8-4c5c-bb59-ff086506cda5/google-search-most-trusted-brands.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/e9176f63-71d8-4c5c-bb59-ff086506cda5/google-search-most-trusted-brands.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/e9176f63-71d8-4c5c-bb59-ff086506cda5/google-search-most-trusted-brands.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/e9176f63-71d8-4c5c-bb59-ff086506cda5/google-search-most-trusted-brands.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Google search for ‘the most trusted brands in the world’ with a highlight around a page on the Morning Consult website\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      A Google search for ‘the most trusted brands in the world’. (Source: <a href='https://www.google.com/'>Google</a>) (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/e9176f63-71d8-4c5c-bb59-ff086506cda5/google-search-most-trusted-brands.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>For the most part, the meta titles are all fine as you can see them in full or, at the very least, get the gist of what the page is about and how it answers the search’s intent.</p>\n\n<p>The descriptions aren’t that great, though, as some are nonsensical and some are incomplete. Both qualities demonstrate that the people behind the site didn’t care enough to write a helpful description for it. Authoritative figures are going to care about stuff like this.</p>\n\n<p>One reason why is because it makes it harder for them to figure out which sites to look deeper into. It’s a pain having to review every top-ranking page because no details are provided to help weed out the so-so from the great. Also, if metadata isn’t filled in, the page might not look all that great when shared on social media, again requiring the sharer to do more work and clean it up.</p>\n\n<p>Let me show you an example:</p>\n\n<p>This is what MozBar reports to me from the <a href=\"https://morningconsult.com/most-trusted-brands/\">Morning Consult</a> page that ranks #2 for this search query:</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/3868fae1-3d87-4ed3-8734-a733d0acc8be/morningconsult-metadata.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/3868fae1-3d87-4ed3-8734-a733d0acc8be/morningconsult-metadata.png analysis of on-page elements and metadata for Morning Consult page\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      MozBar reveals how the metadata was prepared for this page on the Morning Consult website. (Source: <a href='https://morningconsult.com/most-trusted-brands/'>Morning Consult</a>) (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/3868fae1-3d87-4ed3-8734-a733d0acc8be/morningconsult-metadata.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>The page title includes a bunch of icons that thankfully don’t appear in search results. The meta description, however, doesn’t exist. This is why when Google tried to retrieve a description about the page, it created this mess from the report’s findings:</p>\n\n<blockquote>“USPS. Score: 42.0% Amazon. 38.8% Google. 37.9% PayPal. 36.5% Chick-Fil-A. 36.2% The Hershey Company. 36.1% UPS. 36.1% Cheerios. Dove. 34.1% Tide. 34.1% Ziploc. 33.8% Clorox. USPS. Score: 42.0% Amazon. 38.8% Google. 37.9% PayPal. Chick-Fil-A. 36.2% The Hershey Company. 36.1% UPS. 36.1% Cheerios. Dove. 34.1% Tide. 34.1% ...”</blockquote>\n\n<p>That might be enough to keep someone from clicking into the site, believing that if the metadata is this messy, the page is too.</p>\n\n<p>As for the shareability piece, the lack of metadata causes issues, too. Here’s what this page looks like on Facebook, LinkedIn and Twitter (in that order):</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/e4379348-39a5-491f-9a9b-01ca9a3d7619/morningconsult-socialmedia-links.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/e4379348-39a5-491f-9a9b-01ca9a3d7619/morningconsult-socialmedia-links.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Three views of the Morning Consult report when shared on Facebook (top-left), LinkedIn (top-right) and Twitter (bottom-left)\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Three views of the Morning Consult report when shared on Facebook (top-left), LinkedIn (top-right) and Twitter (bottom-left). (Source: <a href='https://morningconsult.com/most-trusted-brands/'>Morning Consult</a>) (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/e4379348-39a5-491f-9a9b-01ca9a3d7619/morningconsult-socialmedia-links.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>Two of the shares pull in the brand logo and tagline, but not the featured image of the page. Two of the shares show no description at all while the other shows a snippet of the first sentence on the page.</p>\n\n<p>Again, this lack of attention to detail ends up creating more work for the sharer, which might be reason enough for them not to share it. Or not to share anything from that website again.</p>\n\n<p>One last thing you can do to make your pages look more link-worthy in search is to use schema markup. The #1 page (from <a href=\"https://blog.infegy.com/who-are-the-worlds-most-trusted-brands-and-why\">Infegy</a>) for “the most trusted brands in the world” did a good job of this (in addition to writing their metadata). The results look great:</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/566428b4-6d9f-4b6d-88f3-9ce6cd36f896/googlesearch-featuredsnippet.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/566428b4-6d9f-4b6d-88f3-9ce6cd36f896/googlesearch-featuredsnippet.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/566428b4-6d9f-4b6d-88f3-9ce6cd36f896/googlesearch-featuredsnippet.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/566428b4-6d9f-4b6d-88f3-9ce6cd36f896/googlesearch-featuredsnippet.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/566428b4-6d9f-4b6d-88f3-9ce6cd36f896/googlesearch-featuredsnippet.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/566428b4-6d9f-4b6d-88f3-9ce6cd36f896/googlesearch-featuredsnippet.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/566428b4-6d9f-4b6d-88f3-9ce6cd36f896/googlesearch-featuredsnippet.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"A Google featured snippet result for the query ‘the most trusted brands in the world’ - from Infegy and displays chart with the top ranks and positive trust %\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      A Google featured snippet result for the query ‘the most trusted brands in the world’. (Source: <a href='https://www.google.com/'>Google</a>) (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/566428b4-6d9f-4b6d-88f3-9ce6cd36f896/googlesearch-featuredsnippet.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>If I needed this data for an article I was writing today, I’d probably end up focusing most of my efforts on this piece since it’s clear that the page and its metadata were so carefully built by its creators.</p>\n\n<p>To recap: There are three things you should pay attention to when setting up link-worthy pages of your site for search:</p>\n\n<ul>\n<li>Include complete SEO metadata.</li>\n<li>Attach a featured image to the page that’s relevant and descriptive.</li>\n<li>Use schema markup whenever possible.</li>\n</ul>\n\n<h3 id=\"wrapping-up\">Wrapping Up</h3>\n\n<p>You might not be too concerned with backlinks, but the owners of your websites certainly are or will be once they catch wind of the power they wield in Google. While a lot of the linkability of a page does depend on the quality of the content, certain design choices you make can affect it as well. So, add these strategies to your SEO-friendly design processes and help your clients claim those highly coveted top-ranking spots.</p>\n\n<div class=\"signature\">\n  <img src=\"https://www.smashingmagazine.com/images/logo/logo--red.png\" alt=\"Smashing Editorial\">\n  <span>(ra, yk, il)</span>\n</div>\n\n\n              </article>\n            </body>\n 23:59:05","updatedTime":"2020-08-23 23:59:05","title":"Inspired Design Decisions With Bradbury Thompson: The Art Of Graphic Design","link":"https://www.smashingmagazine.com/2020/08/inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson/","description":"\n          <html>\n            <head>\n              <meta charset=\"utf-8\">\n              <link rel=\"canonical\" href=\"https://www.smashingmagazine.com/2020/08/inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson/\" />\n              <title>Inspired Design Decisions With Bradbury Thompson: The Art Of Graphic Design</title>\n            </head>\n            <body>\n              <article>\n                <header>\n                  <h1>Inspired Design Decisions With Bradbury Thompson: The Art Of Graphic Design</h1>\n                  \n                    \n                    <address>Andrew Clarke</address>\n                  \n                  <time datetime=\"2020-08-18T10:00:00&#43;00:00\" class=\"op-published\">2020-08-18T10:00:00+00:00</time>\n                  <time datetime=\"2020-08-18T10:00:00&#43;00:00\" class=\"op-modified\">2020-08-23T15:35:52+00:00</time>\n                </header>\n                \n\n<p>The idea for this series &#8212; and the book which will follow it &#8212; was sparked by a casual conversation, but writing it has had a profound impact on me and the work I make for the web.</p>\n\n<p>I’m more thoughtful in my approach to page layout and to the ways a page and its content adapt to different screen sizes. I have a far greater understanding of how composition helps communication and can improve the stories I tell about my clients’ businesses, products, or services.</p>\n\n<p>I discovered how to better create a rhythm which flows from page to page. I learned how that rhythm produces more attractive visual designs and engaging experiences, and how flexible even the simplest grids can be when approached with imagination.</p>\n\n<p>I became fascinated by the ways magazine art directors including Alexey Brodovitch and Bea Feitler brought images and text together. My knowledge of typography developed alongside my enthusiasm for expressive and entertaining type. I’m unlikely ever to make type as beautiful as Herb Lubalin, or as challenging as Neville Brody, but I am more confident to experiment.</p>\n\n<p>This project gave me the confidence to &#8212; as Ruth Ansel suggested &#8212; “step outside of what is expected,” make confident choices, and and to trust my instincts when something feels right. I learned how to channel my often rebellious attitude to conventional design thinking to develop novel solutions to often everyday design problems.</p>\n\n<p>We work in an industry which is now more dominated by the academic, mechanical, and technical aspects of design. Developing this series has reinforced for me that while those activities matter, as Giovanni Pintori wrote, we “need logic and imagination in equal measure.”</p>\n\n<p>As Neville Brody explained, “Once you have broken down the rules, literally anything is possible.” Unconventional thinking needn’t come at the expense of usability. Learning how people interact with a website or use a product shouldn’t dictate a design but instead provide a platform on which to develop engaging, entertaining, and ultimately more memorable experiences.</p>\n\n<p>Learning about the work of designers from different eras and various fields not only inspired my own ideas, it gave me enthusiasm to learn more. Finding new sources of inspiration has become an almost daily obsession, and while my studio walls might not yet be as full as Ruth Ansel’s and Bea Feitler’s, my bookcases, coffee tables, and desk are almost overflowing with my collection of design books.</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/bb688405-8701-4750-880b-59fc0142f131/issue-12-01-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/bb688405-8701-4750-880b-59fc0142f131/issue-12-01-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/bb688405-8701-4750-880b-59fc0142f131/issue-12-01-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/bb688405-8701-4750-880b-59fc0142f131/issue-12-01-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Left: W is for War spread designed by Bradbury Thompson, 1952. Right: America at War spread designed by Bradbury Thompson.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Left: W is for War spread designed by Bradbury Thompson, 1952. Right: America at War spread designed by Bradbury Thompson. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/bb688405-8701-4750-880b-59fc0142f131/issue-12-01-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>For a long time, I had a nagging feeling the web can so much more than we’re making it. Every one of the designers I’ve featured throughout this series challenged perceptions, influenced the direction of their medium, and ultimately inspired others—myself included—to create better work. I hope in some small way, this series can do the same.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"inspired-by-bradbury-thompson\">Inspired By Bradbury Thompson</h3>\n\n<p>Studying one of the most accomplished art directors and graphic designers of the last century seems like a fitting close to this series.</p>\n\n<p>Bradbury Thompson was born in Kansas in 1911, and while he may not have been the best-known, there’s no doubt he was one of the most influential. Thompson studied at Washburn College in his home city of Topeka. From early on, he was inspired by print designs, especially magazines, and used this influence to design the college’s yearbooks.</p>\n\n<p>After graduating from Washburn, Thompson worked for five years at Capper Publications, a local printing company. This first job as a printshop junior wouldn’t have been glamorous, but it gave Thompson a broad knowledge of design and printing techniques which he would use throughout his long career.</p>\n\n\n  <div data-component=\"FeaturePanel\" data-audience=\"non-subscriber\" data-remove=\"true\" class=\"feature-panel-container hidden\"></div>\n\n\n<p>Kansas in the 1930s was well-known for its severe dust storms, but not as a creative centre, so in 1938 Thompson travelled the 1,200 miles east to New York City. Incredibly, for a young man fresh off the road from Kansas, one of his first projects was designing the 1939 World’s Fair catalogue.</p>\n\n<p>Thompson worked for Rogers-Kellogg-Stillson—the printing firm responsible for that World’s Fair—and was assigned to work on Westvaco Inspirations for Printers. This series of promotional booklets were published by Westvaco Corporation to showcase its line of printing papers. Each issue consisted of just sixteen pages, but gave Thomson a “rare opportunity for experimentation provided a receptive designer.”</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/3d96ba3c-79d6-4e8d-b78e-d14e554ce906/issue-12-02-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/3d96ba3c-79d6-4e8d-b78e-d14e554ce906/issue-12-02-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/3d96ba3c-79d6-4e8d-b78e-d14e554ce906/issue-12-02-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/3d96ba3c-79d6-4e8d-b78e-d14e554ce906/issue-12-02-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/3d96ba3c-79d6-4e8d-b78e-d14e554ce906/issue-12-02-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/3d96ba3c-79d6-4e8d-b78e-d14e554ce906/issue-12-02-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"C Stands for Constitution designed by Bradbury Thompson.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      C Stands for Constitution designed by Bradbury Thompson. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/3d96ba3c-79d6-4e8d-b78e-d14e554ce906/issue-12-02-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>Westvaco had published Inspirations since the 1920s and was already widely circulated to an audience of 35,000 agencies, museums, printers, schools, and universities.</p>\n\n<p>Thomson was given no budget to commission original artwork or photographs for the publication, but instead of letting this limit his ideas, he used it as an opportunity to be creative. Inspirations gave Thomson the freedom to experiment with ideas and techniques, and to explore creative concepts. He became “one of the best scroungers in my profession” by borrowing printed plates and separations from agencies, magazines, and even museums, to incorporate into his work.</p>\n\n<p>These borrowed elements included historical photographs and illustrations which Thomson combined with contemporary typography and modern process colors. For Victory, a spread for Inspirations in 1953, Thomson incorporated arrow illustrations and integrated them into targets made from solid colors. He borrowed elements from folk and primitive art, turning them into original works which blended modern with traditional. Working on Inspirations stimulated Thompson’s creativity, and he went on to design over 60 editions.</p>\n\n<p>During WW2, Thompson designed the final few issues of two wartime magazines—Victory and USA—which were published by the Office of War Information. Then in 1945 he became art director of Mademoiselle magazine and stayed in the role for the next fifteen years.</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/416d0840-b415-4f94-884d-25e2f3c587bf/issue-12-03-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/416d0840-b415-4f94-884d-25e2f3c587bf/issue-12-03-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/416d0840-b415-4f94-884d-25e2f3c587bf/issue-12-03-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/416d0840-b415-4f94-884d-25e2f3c587bf/issue-12-03-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/416d0840-b415-4f94-884d-25e2f3c587bf/issue-12-03-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/416d0840-b415-4f94-884d-25e2f3c587bf/issue-12-03-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/416d0840-b415-4f94-884d-25e2f3c587bf/issue-12-03-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Victory spread designed by Bradbury Thompson, 1953.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Victory spread designed by Bradbury Thompson, 1953. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/416d0840-b415-4f94-884d-25e2f3c587bf/issue-12-03-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>The eclectic tendencies Thompson had developed working on Inspirations continued at Mademoiselle and now with a budget to work with, he commissioned up-and-coming artists Andy Warhol, Joan Miro, Willem de Kooning, and my personal favourite pop artist Jasper Johns to illustrate for its fiction section.</p>\n\n<p>Thomson’s magazine work didn’t begin or end with Mademoiselle and throughout his career he work on over thirty more including Business Week, the Harvard Business Review, and Smithsonian magazine.</p>\n\n<p>Bradbury Thompson may not be among the most famous graphic designers but he was widely recognised in the his industry, receiving all three major design awards and more. His awards included the National Society of Art Directors of the Year Award (1950) and the AIGA Medal (1975.) In 1977 Thompson was inducted into Art Directors Club Hall of Fame, and during the 1980s he won first the Frederic W. Goudy Award and then the Type Director’s Club Medal.</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/77dc9dd1-4cbc-44a0-bed2-9246ee6526ab/issue-12-04-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/77dc9dd1-4cbc-44a0-bed2-9246ee6526ab/issue-12-04-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/77dc9dd1-4cbc-44a0-bed2-9246ee6526ab/issue-12-04-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,\n\t\t\t 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/77dc9dd1-4cbc-44a0-bed2-9246ee6526ab/issue-12-04-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/77dc9dd1-4cbc-44a0-bed2-9246ee6526ab/issue-12-04-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/77dc9dd1-4cbc-44a0-bed2-9246ee6526ab/issue-12-04-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Horsepower spread designed by Bradbury Thompson.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Horsepower spread designed by Bradbury Thompson. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/77dc9dd1-4cbc-44a0-bed2-9246ee6526ab/issue-12-04-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>From his earliest experiences working in Topeka, Thompson was a details-orientated designer who paid attention to the finest details in his typography and to the precise cropping and placement of his images. His clever use of often simple palettes of process colors along with black-and-white historical illustrations and geometric forms made his work at the same time classic and contemporary.</p>\n\n<blockquote>\n<p>Type is a thing of constant interest to me. In short, type can be a tool, a toy, and a teacher. It can provide a means of livelihood, a hobby for relaxation, an intellectual stimulant—and a spiritual satisfaction. I believe an avid interest in type necessarily includes a zest for everyday life.<br />&#8212; Bradbury Thompson</p>\n</blockquote>\n\n<p>Like architecture, typography is a blend of beauty with functional utility and Thompson’s designs often combined unusual typographic arrangements with colorful shapes. For Rain, Rain, Rain &#8212; a spread for Mademoiselle magazine in 1958 &#8212; he reproduced the same raincoat wearing figure carrying an umbrella as five colored silhouettes.</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/af583674-7928-4f6b-a9d2-fd5251c156af/issue-12-05-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/af583674-7928-4f6b-a9d2-fd5251c156af/issue-12-05-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/af583674-7928-4f6b-a9d2-fd5251c156af/issue-12-05-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/af583674-7928-4f6b-a9d2-fd5251c156af/issue-12-05-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Rain, Rain, Rain spread designed by Bradbury Thompson, 1958.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Rain, Rain, Rain spread designed by Bradbury Thompson, 1958. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/af583674-7928-4f6b-a9d2-fd5251c156af/issue-12-05-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>In Futural &#8212; a spread for Westvaco Inspirations for Printers in 1962 &#8212; Thompson mirrored the simplified shapes of aeroplanes across pages, using line-work on the verso and solid colors on the recto. He regularly overprinted his colorful shapes to add depth and interest to his designs.</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2fefcb8e-8d4b-40cc-98e6-c1b0ffef2791/issue-12-06-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2fefcb8e-8d4b-40cc-98e6-c1b0ffef2791/issue-12-06-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2fefcb8e-8d4b-40cc-98e6-c1b0ffef2791/issue-12-06-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Futural spread designed by Bradbury Thompson, 1962.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Futural spread designed by Bradbury Thompson, 1962. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2fefcb8e-8d4b-40cc-98e6-c1b0ffef2791/issue-12-06-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>Using his experience of printing technologies, Thompson’s signature designs often use just four process colors. In offset printing, process colors are comprised of percentages of cyan, magenta, yellow, and key (black) inks (CMYK). This process of four-color printing is capable of producing a wide range of colors.</p>\n\n<p>Thompson’s best-known designs often use these colors in their purest form. He frequently separated the colors and printed them in different areas in his compositions. We use the RGB model when we design for screens, but separating those three colors in the way Thompson separated component CMYK colors can create inspiring designs for the web.</p>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ec042da6-0bb6-4382-85e0-a1da6982a12b/issue-12-07-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ec042da6-0bb6-4382-85e0-a1da6982a12b/issue-12-07-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ec042da6-0bb6-4382-85e0-a1da6982a12b/issue-12-07-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"R Stands for Rightous spread designed by Bradbury Thompson.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      R Stands for Rightous spread designed by Bradbury Thompson. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ec042da6-0bb6-4382-85e0-a1da6982a12b/issue-12-07-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>Thompson taught graphic design at Yale University’s School of Art from 1956 until his death in Connecticut in 1995.</p>\n\n<p>The New York Times Book Review said that his artistic autobiography, “The Art of Graphic Design,” was a book in which “art and design are gloriously and daringly mixed”, which is a good representation of his design strategy in general. “The Art of Graphic Design,” was published 1988. While the original hardcover copy I’d like for my collection is now prohibitively expensive, reprinted paperback versions are available at more realistic prices.</p>\n\n<h3 id=\"processing-the-color-palette\">Processing The Color Palette</h3>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a
