2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/b3a454dd-c463-4d58-80f6-d5c2d163d43c/issue-12-08-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"For this first design, I chose a CMYK inspired palette using darker tints of cyan, magenta, and yellow for better results on screen.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      For this first design, I chose a CMYK inspired palette using darker tints of cyan, magenta, and yellow for better results on screen. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/b3a454dd-c463-4d58-80f6-d5c2d163d43c/issue-12-08-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>I start implementing this first design by first considering my content, then the most appropriate HTML elements to describe it. For this Thompson-inspired design, I need only a few elements, a header, article, and aside, plus two figures:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-html\">&#60;header&#62;\n  &#60;svg id=\"logo\"&#62;…&#60;/svg&#62;\n  &#60;h1&#62;…&#60;/h1&#62;\n  &#60;svg id=\"banner\"&#62;…&#60;/svg&#62;\n  &#60;/div&#62;\n&#60;/header&#62;\n\n&#60;article&#62;\n  &#60;main&#62;…&#60;/main&#62;\n&#60;/article&#62;\n\n&#60;figure&#62;…&#60;/figure&#62;\n&#60;aside&#62;…&#60;/aside&#62;\n&#60;figure&#62;…&#60;/figure&#62;\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>As I’ve discussed throughout this series, my process always starts by applying foundation styles, which include colors and typography. I add a deep blue background color and contrasting white serif text:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">body {\npadding: 2rem 0;\nbackground-color: #1f455f;\nfont-family: 'serif';\ncolor: #fff; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>I style my italic headlines, then add sizes for the heading levels and paragraphs:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">h1, h2 {\nfont-style: italic; }\n\nh1 {\nfont-size: 2.8rem; }\n\nh2 {\nfont-size: 2.027rem; }\n\np {\nfont-size: .8rem; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Finally, I color the captions which accompany both my figures’ images with a vibrant green and italicise the text to match my headline styles:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">figcaption {\nfont-size: .8rem;\nfont-style: italic;\ntext-align: center;\ncolor: #d2de4a; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a1b4b180-a256-48f2-ac6a-fce6770740f0/issue-12-09-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a1b4b180-a256-48f2-ac6a-fce6770740f0/issue-12-09-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a1b4b180-a256-48f2-ac6a-fce6770740f0/issue-12-09-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a1b4b180-a256-48f2-ac6a-fce6770740f0/issue-12-09-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a1b4b180-a256-48f2-ac6a-fce6770740f0/issue-12-09-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a1b4b180-a256-48f2-ac6a-fce6770740f0/issue-12-09-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a1b4b180-a256-48f2-ac6a-fce6770740f0/issue-12-09-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"design in RGB (red, green, and blue)\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a1b4b180-a256-48f2-ac6a-fce6770740f0/issue-12-09-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<h4 id=\"cmyk-in-rgb\">CMYK in RGB</h4>\n\n<p>To produce CMYK process colors—cyan, magenta, yellow, and key (black) in RGB (red, green, and blue) for screens, use maximum values for two out of those colors. If the result is too hard on the eyes, add black to create tints and soften the effect.</p>\n\n<p>On even the smallest screens, some space needs to remain empty. This allows the eye to flow around content. Margins and padding are often all that’s needed to add empty space:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">#logo {\nmargin: 0 auto 1rem; }\n\n#banner {\nmargin: 1rem 1rem 1rem 0; }\n\nmain, aside {\nmargin: 0 1rem; }\n\nfigure {\nmargin: 2rem auto; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Reducing the maximum width of graphic elements adds white-space and visual interest to small-screen designs:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">#logo {\nmax-width: 25vw; }\n\nfigure {\nmax-width: 50vw; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2a792e26-ec87-4718-a133-07f7dd6eeac3/issue-12-10-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2a792e26-ec87-4718-a133-07f7dd6eeac3/issue-12-10-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2a792e26-ec87-4718-a133-07f7dd6eeac3/issue-12-10-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2a792e26-ec87-4718-a133-07f7dd6eeac3/issue-12-10-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2a792e26-ec87-4718-a133-07f7dd6eeac3/issue-12-10-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2a792e26-ec87-4718-a133-07f7dd6eeac3/issue-12-10-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2a792e26-ec87-4718-a133-07f7dd6eeac3/issue-12-10-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Before implementing any design, I often make a storyboard to demonstrate how my elements will flow across a selection of screen sizes.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Before implementing any design, I often make a storyboard to demonstrate how my elements will flow across a selection of screen sizes. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2a792e26-ec87-4718-a133-07f7dd6eeac3/issue-12-10-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>The extra space available on medium-size screens allows me to introduce the first set of layout styles to this design. By splitting my running text across two columns, I help to maintain consistency in its measure. Placing my two figures, side-by-side maintains their relative proportions to my text.</p>\n\n<p>I start by applying grid properties and an unusual five-column symmetrical grid to the body element. Then, I add a data URI background image and position it to the right of my layout:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">@media (min-width: 48em) {\n\nbody {\ndisplay: grid;\ngrid-template-columns: repeat(5, 1fr);\ngap: 2rem;\nbackground-image: url(\"data:image/svg+xml…\");\nbackground-position: 120% 50%;\nbackground-repeat: no-repeat; }\n}\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>I need to place the content of my header and article directly onto my grid, so I change those elements’ display property to contents, which effectively removes them for styling purposes:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">header, article {\ndisplay: contents; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Then, I place each content elements into a different set of grid columns and rows using line numbers. First, I place the Ford logo into a single column. I can remove the maximum width I set earlier as its size will now depend on the width of its column:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">#logo {\ngrid-column: 2;\nmargin: 0;\nmax-width: none; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>The banner contains a Transit van profile, and the main headline occupies the first four of my five columns:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">#banner, \nh1 {\ngrid-column: 1 / 4; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>By leaving the first column empty, content in the main and aside elements are indented from the left. By setting their widths to match that of my banner, I add a pleasing asymmetry to the layout:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">main, aside {\ngrid-column: 2 / -1; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Although my two figures are’t adjacent elements in my HTML, CSS Grid makes placing them side-by-side simple. I place them into different columns on the same row without needing to alter my HTML:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">figure:nth-of-type(1) {\ngrid-column: 2 / 4;\ngrid-row: 5; }\n\nfigure:nth-of-type(2) {\ngrid-column: 4 / -1;\ngrid-row: 5; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>In many of my designs, I use indentation instead of paragraph spacing to create solid blocks from my running text. This effect is even more striking when setting text in multiple columns:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">p {\nmargin-bottom: 0; }\n\np + p {\ntext-indent: 2ch; }\n\nmain {\ncolumn-width: 16em; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Figure elements can include one or more captions and images. Captions commonly appear under the pictures they describe, but there’s no reason captions need to stay underneath. I can place them above, or to the left or right of an image too.</p>\n\n<p>When I place captions on either the left or right of an image, I immediately give designs the look of a magazine. I use Flexbox and then the flex-direction property to move them:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">figure {\ndisplay: flex; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>My first figure caption appear on the left, so I reverse the flex-direction of this figure from its default row:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">figure:nth-of-type(1) {\nflex-direction: row-reverse; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Flexbox allows me to arrange elements vertically as well as horizontally. To place my captions at the bottom edge of my images, I change their cross-axis alignment from the default stretch to flex-end:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">figure {\nalign-items: flex-end; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>For a finishing touch to this medium-size design, I align both captions in opposite directions:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">figure:nth-of-type(1) figcaption {\ntext-align: right; }\n\nfigure:nth-of-type(2) figcaption {\ntext-align: left; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/1d4706f6-71bf-4b03-a918-0820e476e224/issue-12-11-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/1d4706f6-71bf-4b03-a918-0820e476e224/issue-12-11-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/1d4706f6-71bf-4b03-a918-0820e476e224/issue-12-11-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/1d4706f6-71bf-4b03-a918-0820e476e224/issue-12-11-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/1d4706f6-71bf-4b03-a918-0820e476e224/issue-12-11-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/1d4706f6-71bf-4b03-a918-0820e476e224/issue-12-11-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/1d4706f6-71bf-4b03-a918-0820e476e224/issue-12-11-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Overlapping four and six columns creates this compound grid.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Overlapping four and six columns creates this compound grid. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/1d4706f6-71bf-4b03-a918-0820e476e224/issue-12-11-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>Empty space helps to lead the eye at every stage of this layout. The extra space available on larger screens allows me to develop a distinctive asymmetric design.</p>\n\n<p>Using a compound grid—two or more overlapping or stacked grids—on one page can create eye-catching compositions. The compound grid for this design overlaps a four-column and six-column grid which creates a rhythmic pattern of 2|1|1|2. I transfer that pattern to fr units and apply them as columns to the body element:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">@media (min-width: 64em) {\n\nbody {\ngrid-template-columns: 2fr 1fr 1fr 2fr 2fr 1fr 1fr 2fr; }\n}\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Then, I add four rows using a combination of pixels, rem units, and intrinsic sizing, before setting the minimum height of the page to fill the viewport:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">body {\ngrid-template-rows: 100px 14rem 14rem auto;\nmin-height: 100vh; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>To complete the body styles, I add two new data URI background images and specify their sizes so they’re always contained within the viewport:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">body {\nbackground-image:\nurl(\"data:image/svg+xml…\"),\nurl(\"data:image/svg+xml…\");\nbackground-position: 0 50%, 100% 50%;\nbackground-size: contain; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca1ca11d-0992-4bfb-aff9-71d7e3bb71d1/issue-12-12-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca1ca11d-0992-4bfb-aff9-71d7e3bb71d1/issue-12-12-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca1ca11d-0992-4bfb-aff9-71d7e3bb71d1/issue-12-12-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca1ca11d-0992-4bfb-aff9-71d7e3bb71d1/issue-12-12-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca1ca11d-0992-4bfb-aff9-71d7e3bb71d1/issue-12-12-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca1ca11d-0992-4bfb-aff9-71d7e3bb71d1/issue-12-12-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca1ca11d-0992-4bfb-aff9-71d7e3bb71d1/issue-12-12-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"This asymmetric design is highly structured, and every element is placed precisely onto my grid.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      This asymmetric design is highly structured, and every element is placed precisely onto my grid. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ca1ca11d-0992-4bfb-aff9-71d7e3bb71d1/issue-12-12-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>This asymmetric design is highly structured, and every element is precisely placed onto my grid. I use line numbers to place the structural elements, raising the overlapping headline above the banner image in the stacking order:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">#logo {\ngrid-column: 2 / 4;\ngrid-row: 1; }\n\nh1 {\ngrid-column: 1 / 5;\ngrid-row: 2 / 4;\nalign-self: center;\nz-index: 2; }\n\n#banner {\ngrid-column: 1 / 5;\ngrid-row: 2 / 4;\nz-index: 1; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>My main content occupies the last two columns and forms and island in the right of this design:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">main {\ngrid-column: 7 / -1;\ngrid-row: 2 / 4;\ncolumn-width: auto; }\n\naside {\ngrid-column: 6 / -1;\ngrid-row: 4 / 5; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>I place the two figures onto this new grid:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">figure:nth-of-type(1) {\ngrid-column: 5 / 6;\ngrid-row: 2 / 3; }\n\nfigure:nth-of-type(2) {\ngrid-column: 2 / 5;\ngrid-row: 4 / 5; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Then, I adjust the direction of their flex, setting the first figure vertically, so my caption appears above its sibling image:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">figure:nth-of-type(1) {\nflex-direction: column-reverse; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>The content of my second figure is arranged horizontally with both the image and caption resting on the baseline:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">figure:nth-of-type(2) {\nflex-direction: row;\nalign-items: flex-end; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>I fine-tune the alignment of both caption and this first Thompson-inspired design is complete:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">figure:nth-of-type(1) figcaption {\ntext-align: center; }\n\nfigure:nth-of-type(2) figcaption {\nflex: 1;\ntext-align: left; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"sponsors__lead-place\"></div>\n\n\n\n\n<h3 id=\"colorfully-complementary\">Colorfully Complementary</h3>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2ef24ab4-0ae6-4f3f-a413-6e746285ffcb/issue-12-14-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"This colorfully complementary header is the centrepiece of my design for medium and large screens.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      This colorfully complementary header is the centrepiece of my design for medium and large screens. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2ef24ab4-0ae6-4f3f-a413-6e746285ffcb/issue-12-14-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>Despite the apparent complexity of this layout, I need only three structural elements in my HTML: a header which contains Transit vans in a variety of complementary colors, then two content elements, a main and an aside:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-html\">&#60;header&#62;…&#60;/header&#62;\n\n&#60;main&#62;…&#60;/main&#62;\n\n&#60;aside&#62;…&#60;/aside&#62;\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>A colorfully complementary header is the centrepiece of this design. It might be tempting to implement this using a single large image. But, I want to develop various arrangements for different screen sizes, so using nine separate images allows me to make a scrolling panel for small screens, and arrange them in a grid for medium and large screens:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-html\">&#60;header&#62;\n  &#60;img src=\"header-1.svg\" alt=\"Ford Transit\"&#62;\n  &#60;img src=\"header-2.svg\" alt=\"\"&#62;\n  &#60;img src=\"header-3.svg\" alt=\"\"&#62;\n  …\n  &#60;img src=\"header-9.svg\" alt=\"\"&#62;\n&#60;/header&#62;\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/b996bcb0-7986-4e51-a58b-a5862d95e7f0/issue-12-15-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/b996bcb0-7986-4e51-a58b-a5862d95e7f0/issue-12-15-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"In a split complementary palette, two colors on either side of the complementary on the color wheel are used. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/b996bcb0-7986-4e51-a58b-a5862d95e7f0/issue-12-15-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>Both the main and aside elements include a headline, an exploded Transit parts SVG image, plus divisions for arranging my content into columns:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-html\">&#60;main&#62;\n  &#60;h1&#62;…&#60;/h1&#62;\n  &#60;div&#62;…&#60;/div&#62;\n  &#60;div&#62;…&#60;/div&#62;\n  &#60;svg&#62;…&#60;/svg&#62;\n&#60;/main&#62;\n\n&#60;aside&#62;\n  &#60;h2&#62;…&#60;/h2&#62;\n  &#60;div&#62;…&#60;/div&#62;\n  &#60;div&#62;…&#60;/div&#62;\n  &#60;svg&#62;…&#60;/svg&#62;\n&#60;/aside&#62;\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>I start by applying a dark grey background color to the body element, and add stying to my headlines and paragraphs:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">body {\nbackground-color: #262626;\nfont-family: 'sans-serif';\ncolor: #fff; }\n\nh1, h2 {\nfont-size: 2.027rem;\nfont-style: italic;\ntext-transform: uppercase; }\n\np {\nfont-size: .8rem; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/936ff96f-3bbf-458e-b2ff-404b2c2fb38e/issue-12-16-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/936ff96f-3bbf-458e-b2ff-404b2c2fb38e/issue-12-16-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/936ff96f-3bbf-458e-b2ff-404b2c2fb38e/issue-12-16-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/936ff96f-3bbf-458e-b2ff-404b2c2fb38e/issue-12-16-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/936ff96f-3bbf-458e-b2ff-404b2c2fb38e/issue-12-16-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/936ff96f-3bbf-458e-b2ff-404b2c2fb38e/issue-12-16-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/936ff96f-3bbf-458e-b2ff-404b2c2fb38e/issue-12-16-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"On small screens, the main and aside elements get grid layout too.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      On small screens, the main and aside elements get grid layout too. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/936ff96f-3bbf-458e-b2ff-404b2c2fb38e/issue-12-16-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>Often, normal flow plus a few foundation styles are all I need to implement a small-screen version of my designs, but this one includes layout styles from the start. I begin by transforming my header and its nine images into a horizontally scrolling panel by adding flex and overflow properties:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">header {\ndisplay: flex;\noverflow-x: scroll;\nmargin: 0 2rem 2rem; }\n\nheader img:not(:last-of-type) {\nmargin-right: 1rem; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>The header isn’t the only element to get a layout on small screens, the main and aside elements get grids too:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">main, aside {\ndisplay: grid;\nmargin: 0 2rem; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>First, I apply a two-column layout to the main element. The exploded Transit parts SVG image fit into the right column, so I fix its width at 100px. The left column expands to fill any remaining space.</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">main {\ngrid-template-columns: [content] 1fr [svg] 100px; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Then, I place main element items using grid lines with names which reflect their content:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">h1 {\ngrid-column: content;\ngrid-row: 1; }\n\nmain > div:nth-of-type(1) {\ngrid-column: content;\ngrid-row: 2; }\n\nmain > div:nth-of-type(2) {\ngrid-column: content;\ngrid-row: 3; }\n\nmain > svg {\ngrid-column: svg;\ngrid-row: 1 / 4; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>The aside element also has a two-column layout, but this time the narrow column and its exploded Transit parts are on the left. To emphasise the distinction between my main and aside content areas, I add a solid border at the top of the aside:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">aside {\ngrid-template-columns: [svg] 100px [content] 1fr;\npadding-top: 1rem;\nborder-top: 3px solid #b22f65; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>I use named lines to place its content into my grid:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">h2 {\ngrid-column: 1 / -1;\ngrid-row: 1; }\n\naside > div:nth-of-type(1) {\ngrid-column: content;\ngrid-row: 2; }\n\naside > div:nth-of-type(2) {\ngrid-column: content;\ngrid-row: 3; }\n\naside > div:nth-of-type(3) {\ngrid-column: svg;\ngrid-row: 2 / 4; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>A horizontally scrolling header and grids in my content demonstrate how it’s sometimes beneficial to use more than a single-column layout for small screens. Those same elements can be arranged in very different ways in the extra space available on medium-size screens.</p>\n\n<p>In this version of my design, a grid of nine colorfully complementary images fills the header. I apply grid properties and three symmetrical columns:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">@media (min-width: 48em) {\n\nheader {\ndisplay: grid;\ngrid-template-columns: 1fr 1fr 1fr;\ngap: 1rem;\noverflow-x: visible; }\n}\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/be2ec175-7f5d-444f-b313-c296af24f77e/issue-12-17-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/be2ec175-7f5d-444f-b313-c296af24f77e/issue-12-17-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/be2ec175-7f5d-444f-b313-c296af24f77e/issue-12-17-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/be2ec175-7f5d-444f-b313-c296af24f77e/issue-12-17-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/be2ec175-7f5d-444f-b313-c296af24f77e/issue-12-17-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/be2ec175-7f5d-444f-b313-c296af24f77e/issue-12-17-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/be2ec175-7f5d-444f-b313-c296af24f77e/issue-12-17-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Left: grid-auto-flow with a value of row places elements horizontally across rows. Right: Changing the grid-auto-flow value to column, fills each column vertically.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Left: grid-auto-flow with a value of row places elements horizontally across rows. Right: Changing the grid-auto-flow value to column, fills each column vertically. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/be2ec175-7f5d-444f-b313-c296af24f77e/issue-12-17-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>Unlike other elements in this design, there’s no need to place the images into this grid, as the browser’s auto-placement algorithm arranges them automatically.</p>\n\n<p>By default, browsers place elements horizontally across rows. But, by changing the grid-auto-flow value to column, a browser fills each column vertically before moving onto the next:</p>\n\n<p>With more space available for my content, I increase the number of columns from two to four:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">main, aside {\ngrid-template-columns: 1fr [svg] 1fr 1fr 1fr;\ngap: 2rem; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Then, I align content in my main element to the end, so it forms a solid block in the centre of my layout:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">main {\nalign-items: end; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>My main headline spans all four columns. Although it appears first in my HTML, I can place it visually below my running text and images by adding it to the second row:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">h1 {\ngrid-column: 1 / -1;\ngrid-row: 2;\nborder-bottom: 3px solid #b22f65; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>I place my first block of content into the left column:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">main > div:nth-of-type(1) {\ngrid-column: 1;\ngrid-row: 1; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>The second block spans two columns on the right:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">main > div:nth-of-type(2) {\ngrid-column: 3 / span 2;\ngrid-row: 1; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Next, I place the final division—which contains my SVG image &#8212; into the second column using its line name:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">main > div:nth-of-type(3) {\ngrid-column: svg;\ngrid-row: 1; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Implementing columns for the aside element follows a similar method. Again, I alter the visual placement of my headline using row line numbers:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">h2 {\ngrid-column: 3 / -1;\ngrid-row: 2; }\n\naside > div:nth-of-type(1) {\ngrid-column: 1;\ngrid-row: 1 / 3; }\n\naside > div:nth-of-type(2) {\ngrid-column: 3 / -1;\ngrid-row: 1; }\n\naside > div:nth-of-type(3) {\ngrid-column: svg;\ngrid-row: 1 / 3; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a6931dab-f63e-4c70-b2fd-e01cab412a83/issue-12-18-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a6931dab-f63e-4c70-b2fd-e01cab412a83/issue-12-18-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a6931dab-f63e-4c70-b2fd-e01cab412a83/issue-12-18-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a6931dab-f63e-4c70-b2fd-e01cab412a83/issue-12-18-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a6931dab-f63e-4c70-b2fd-e01cab412a83/issue-12-18-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a6931dab-f63e-4c70-b2fd-e01cab412a83/issue-12-18-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a6931dab-f63e-4c70-b2fd-e01cab412a83/issue-12-18-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"When you use modular grids thoughtfully they can fill your designs with energy.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      When you use modular grids thoughtfully they can fill your designs with energy. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/a6931dab-f63e-4c70-b2fd-e01cab412a83/issue-12-18-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>A full-page image filling one half of a spread is a common sight in magazine designs. Large images like these can be equally as effective on widescreen displays. I apply grid properties to the body element with two symmetrical columns, then name the left column verso and the right column recto:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">@media (min-width: 64em) {\n\nbody {\ndisplay: grid;\ngrid-template-columns: [verso] 1fr [recto] 1fr;\ngap: 2rem; }\n}\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>These terms originate in Latin where two opposite pages are called folium rectum and folium versum. I place my header into the verso column, and the main and aside elements stack in the recto column:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">header {\ngrid-column: verso;\ngrid-row: 1 / 4; }\n\nmain, aside {\ngrid-column: recto; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/6314f422-1aaf-42ee-85ad-15b3e72198fe/issue-12-19-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/6314f422-1aaf-42ee-85ad-15b3e72198fe/issue-12-19-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png grids help bring order to large amounts of varied content and create visually appealing layouts.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Modular grids help bring order to large amounts of varied content and create visually appealing layouts. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/6314f422-1aaf-42ee-85ad-15b3e72198fe/issue-12-19-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>Finally, to improve the readability of my running text on very wide displays, I introduce a multi-column layout. A browser will automatically generate 10em-wide columns to fill the space available:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">@media (min-width: 72em) {\n\nmain > div:nth-of-type(2),\naside > div:nth-of-type(2) {\ncolumn-width: 10em;\ncolumn-gap: 2rem; }\n}\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"sponsors__lead-place\"></div>\n\n\n\n\n<h3 id=\"masking-scalable-type\">Masking Scalable Type</h3>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/139afc93-7075-41ee-a11d-1d72c36813c7/issue-12-20-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/139afc93-7075-41ee-a11d-1d72c36813c7/issue-12-20-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/139afc93-7075-41ee-a11d-1d72c36813c7/issue-12-20-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/139afc93-7075-41ee-a11d-1d72c36813c7/issue-12-20-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Brightly colored blocks of SVG text add impact in this distinctive design, inspired by Bradbury Thompson.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Brightly colored blocks of SVG text add impact in this distinctive design, inspired by Bradbury Thompson. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/139afc93-7075-41ee-a11d-1d72c36813c7/issue-12-20-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>As someone who enjoys the creative aspects of typographic design &#8212; but also values accessibility and performance &#8212; SVG has become as much a part of my everyday development toolkit as CSS and HTML.</p>\n\n<p>This next Thompson-inspired design combines SVG text with CSS masks and shapes, but needs very little HTML, just one header and a main element:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-html\">&#60;header&#62;\n  &#60;div&#62;\n    &#60;svg&#62;…&#60;/svg&#62;\n  &#60;/div&#62;\n&#60;header&#62;\n\n&#60;main&#62;\n  &#60;svg&#62;…&#60;/svg&#62;\n&#60;/main&#62;\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Before I start developing the striking SVGs, I add foundation styles which give the page a deep blue background color and contrasting white text:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">body {\nbackground-color: #1f455e;\nfont-family: 'sans-serif';\ncolor: #fff; }\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"\n  \n    break-out article__image\n  \n  \n  \">\n  \n    <a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/12ec5e63-ffdf-44f1-9235-86ddf9f1f3bb/issue-12-21-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">\n    \n    <img\n\t\t\tsrcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/12ec5e63-ffdf-44f1-9235-86ddf9f1f3bb/issue-12-21-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/12ec5e63-ffdf-44f1-9235-86ddf9f1f3bb/issue-12-21-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/12ec5e63-ffdf-44f1-9235-86ddf9f1f3bb/issue-12-21-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/12ec5e63-ffdf-44f1-9235-86ddf9f1f3bb/issue-12-21-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,\n\t\t\t        https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/12ec5e63-ffdf-44f1-9235-86ddf9f1f3bb/issue-12-21-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\"\n\t\t\tsrc=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/12ec5e63-ffdf-44f1-9235-86ddf9f1f3bb/issue-12-21-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"\n\t\t\tsizes=\"100vw\"\n\t\t\talt=\"Left: Scalable graphic with repeating text. Center: CSS mask-image uses black and white parts of an image. Right: Repeating text shaped by a Transit van silhouette.\"\n\t\t/>\n    \n    </a>\n  \n\n  \n    <figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\n      Left: Scalable graphic with repeating text. Center: CSS mask-image uses black and white parts of an image. Right: Repeating text shaped by a Transit van silhouette. (<a href='https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/12ec5e63-ffdf-44f1-9235-86ddf9f1f3bb/issue-12-21-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png'>Large preview</a>)\n    </figcaption>\n  \n</figure>\n\n<p>This header includes a scalable graphic where the repeating text is shaped by a Transit van outline. SVG includes its own method for clipping parts of an image. To define a clipping path I add a clipPath element to my SVG. This, in turn, contains a path which defines my clipped area. So I can reference this clipPath later in my SVG, I give it a unique identifier:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-html\">&#60;svg&#62;\n  &#60;clipPath id=\"transit\"&#62;\n    &#60;path&#62;…&#60;/path&#62;\n  &#60;/clipPath&#62;\n&#60;/svg&#62;\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Then, I add the path coordinates which make up my graphical text. I give this group of brightly colored paths a class attribute value which I can use to bind it to my clipPath:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-html\">&#60;svg&#62;\n  &#60;clipPath id=\"transit\"&#62;…&#60;/clipPath&#62;\n    &#60;g class=\"transit\"&#62;\n      &#60;path&#62;…&#60;/path&#62;\n    &#60;/g&#62;\n&#60;/svg&#62;\n</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<p>Whether I include this SVG in my HTML using an image element, or embed the SVG directly into my markup, I use the CSS clip-path property to clip my graphic text using its clipPath:</p>\n\n<div class=\"break-out\">\n<pre><code class=\"language-css\">&#60;style type=\"text/css\"&#62;&#60;![CDATA[\n.transit {\n-webkit-clip-path: url(#transit);\nclip-path: url(#transit); }\n]]&gt;&#60;/style&#62;</code></pre></div><p>Using clipPath, only areas within a clipping path are displayed. Anything outside the clipped area will remain invisible.</p><p>But, there’s another way to mask an element, one which works with all types of content, not just SVG. Similar to clip-path, CSS masks hide parts of an element using a black and white mask image.</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">header div {\n-webkit-mask-image: url(\"mask.svg\");\nmask-image: url(\"mask.svg\"); }</code></pre></div><p>When a mask is applied, only areas of an element which coincide with the black parts of the mask will be displayed. Everything outside these areas will disappear.</p><figure class=\"         \"><a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/c0b07e54-ecff-4a6a-b2ab-6805f43b707d/issue-12-22-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"><img srcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/c0b07e54-ecff-4a6a-b2ab-6805f43b707d/issue-12-22-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/c0b07e54-ecff-4a6a-b2ab-6805f43b707d/issue-12-22-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/c0b07e54-ecff-4a6a-b2ab-6805f43b707d/issue-12-22-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/c0b07e54-ecff-4a6a-b2ab-6805f43b707d/issue-12-22-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/c0b07e54-ecff-4a6a-b2ab-6805f43b707d/issue-12-22-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\" src=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/c0b07e54-ecff-4a6a-b2ab-6805f43b707d/issue-12-22-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\" sizes=\"100vw\" alt=\"Applying an alternative mask image preserves the visual weight of this masked header on smaller screens.\"/></a><figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\nApplying an alternative mask image preserves the visual weight of this masked header on smaller screens. (<a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/c0b07e54-ecff-4a6a-b2ab-6805f43b707d/issue-12-22-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">Large preview</a>)</figcaption></figure><p>The properties of mask-image share many similarities with backgrounds in CSS. Just like background images, masks can be positioned, repeated, and sized, and can even be developed from background gradients. As I don’t need my mask image to repeat, I set its value to no-repeat, just as would with any background image:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">header div {\n-webkit-mask-repeat: no-repeat;\nmask-repeat: no-repeat; }</code></pre></div><figure class=\"        break-out article__image         \"><a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ee016d76-1bd8-42c1-aac6-f4f707d1d5c1/issue-12-23-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"><img srcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ee016d76-1bd8-42c1-aac6-f4f707d1d5c1/issue-12-23-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ee016d76-1bd8-42c1-aac6-f4f707d1d5c1/issue-12-23-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ee016d76-1bd8-42c1-aac6-f4f707d1d5c1/issue-12-23-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ee016d76-1bd8-42c1-aac6-f4f707d1d5c1/issue-12-23-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ee016d76-1bd8-42c1-aac6-f4f707d1d5c1/issue-12-23-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\" src=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ee016d76-1bd8-42c1-aac6-f4f707d1d5c1/issue-12-23-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\" sizes=\"100vw\" alt=\"Brightly colored lines of SVG text styled using CSS.\"/></a><figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\nBrightly colored lines of SVG text styled using CSS. (<a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/ee016d76-1bd8-42c1-aac6-f4f707d1d5c1/issue-12-23-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">Large preview</a>)</figcaption></figure><p>The contents of my SVG in the main element is entirely different. This graphic contains brightly colored lines of SVG text which explain the Transit van’s pedigree. I wrap each line inside a tspan element, each with its own x and y coordinates which tightly pack the text into a solid block:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-html\">&#60;svg&#62;\n&#60;text&#62;\n&#60;tspan x=\"0\" y=\"86\"&#62;BUILT AS A PASSENGER VAN, MINIBUS, &#60;/tspan&#62;\n&#60;tspan x=\"0\" y=\"156\"&#62;CUTAWAY VAN CHASSIS, AND A PICKUP &#60;/tspan&#62;\n&#60;tspan x=\"0\" y=\"226\"&#62;TRUCK. OVER 8,000,000 TRANSIT VANS &#60;/tspan&#62;\n&#60;tspan x=\"0\" y=\"296\"&#62;HAVE BEEN SOLD, MAKING IT THE THIRD &#60;/tspan&#62;\n&#60;tspan x=\"0\" y=\"366\"&#62;BEST-SELLING VAN OF ALL TIME.&#60;/tspan&#62;\n&#60;/text&#62;\n&#60;/svg&#62;</code></pre></div><p>SVG text elements can be styled like any HTML text, so to emphasise the solidity of this block, I choose a heavyweight, condensed sans-serif, then adjust its tracking by reducing the letter spacing by -2px;</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">text {\nfont-family: 'sans-serif-condensed';\nfont-size: 83px;\nfont-weight: 700;\nletter-spacing: -2px; }</code></pre></div><p>CSS pseudo-class selectors are as useful for styling elements in SVG as they are for HTML. I use nth-of-type selectors to give each line of tspan text its own color:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">tspan:nth-of-type(1) {\nfill: #c43d56; }\ntspan:nth-of-type(2) {\nfill: #f2c867; }\ntspan:nth-of-type(3) {\nfill: #377dab; }\ntspan:nth-of-type(4) {\nfill: #fff; }\ntspan:nth-of-type(5) {\nfill: #c43d56; }</code></pre></div><figure class=\"         \"><a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/32f57f0b-74dd-4641-83ee-81924541431a/issue-12-24-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"><img srcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/32f57f0b-74dd-4641-83ee-81924541431a/issue-12-24-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/32f57f0b-74dd-4641-83ee-81924541431a/issue-12-24-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/32f57f0b-74dd-4641-83ee-81924541431a/issue-12-24-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/32f57f0b-74dd-4641-83ee-81924541431a/issue-12-24-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/32f57f0b-74dd-4641-83ee-81924541431a/issue-12-24-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\" src=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/32f57f0b-74dd-4641-83ee-81924541431a/issue-12-24-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\" sizes=\"100vw\" alt=\"In this alternative version of my design for larger screens, I want the paragraph to float alongside the masked graphic.\"/></a><figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\nIn this alternative version of my design for larger screens, I want the paragraph to float alongside the masked graphic. (<a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/32f57f0b-74dd-4641-83ee-81924541431a/issue-12-24-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">Large preview</a>)</figcaption></figure><p>The solid style of this typographic design makes a stylish header element, but there are times when I might need to add more content to this page. For an alternative take on this design, I add a paragraph explaining the history of the Transit van’s production to my header:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-html\">&#60;header&#62;\n&#60;div&#62;\n&#60;svg&#62;…&#60;/svg&#62;\n&#60;/div&#62;\n&#60;p&#62;…&#60;/p&#62;\n&#60;/header&#62;</code></pre></div><p>In my foundation styles, I add a font size and set the paragraph in uppercase to match my previous SVG text:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">header p {\nfont-size: .91rem;\ntext-transform: uppercase; }</code></pre></div><p>Then, I justify the paragraph text for people who use browsers which also support automatic hyphenation:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">@supports (-webkit-hyphens: auto) or (hyphens: auto) {\nheader p {\n-webkit-hyphens: auto;\nhyphens: auto;\ntext-align: justify; }\n}</code></pre></div><p>On small and medium-size screens, this new paragraph of text follows the header’s SVG as it does in the HTML. But, for larger screens, I want this text to float alongside the masked graphic.</p><p>I give the header graphic an explicit viewport-based width, then float it to enable me to wrap my text around it using CSS Shapes. As I want this shape to match my masked graphic, I use the same mask image for the shape-outside URL:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">@media (min-width: 64em) {\nheader div {\nfloat: left;\nwidth: 65vw;\nmargin-bottom: 0;\nshape-outside: url(mask.svg);\nshape-margin: 20px; }\n}</code></pre></div><h3 id=\"splitting-symmetry\">Splitting Symmetry</h3><figure class=\"        break-out article__image         \"><a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/9c9f49de-b0b8-4f59-aeef-c8d112bc3a23/issue-12-25-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"><img srcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/9c9f49de-b0b8-4f59-aeef-c8d112bc3a23/issue-12-25-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/9c9f49de-b0b8-4f59-aeef-c8d112bc3a23/issue-12-25-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/9c9f49de-b0b8-4f59-aeef-c8d112bc3a23/issue-12-25-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/9c9f49de-b0b8-4f59-aeef-c8d112bc3a23/issue-12-25-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/9c9f49de-b0b8-4f59-aeef-c8d112bc3a23/issue-12-25-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\" src=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/9c9f49de-b0b8-4f59-aeef-c8d112bc3a23/issue-12-25-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\" sizes=\"100vw\" alt=\"Bright colors in this Thompson-inspired design help connect the two sides of this symmetrical layout.\"/></a><figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\nBright colors in this Thompson-inspired design help connect the two sides of this symmetrical layout. (<a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/9c9f49de-b0b8-4f59-aeef-c8d112bc3a23/issue-12-25-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">Large preview</a>)</figcaption></figure><p>For the final inspired example in this issue—and in fact for the entire series—the split symmetrical layout means I need just two structural elements. By now, these header and main elements should feel very familiar. My header includes the classic Ford logo, an SVG image and a headline:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-html\">&#60;header&#62;\n&#60;svg id=\"logo\"&#62;…&#60;/svg&#62;\n&#60;img src=\"header.svg\" alt=\"Ford Transit\"&#62;\n&#60;h1&#62;…&#60;/h1&#62;\n&#60;/header&#62;</code></pre></div><p>The main element also includes a scalable image, plus a single paragraph of running text:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-html\">&#60;main&#62;\n&#60;p&#62;…&#60;/p&#62;\n&#60;img src=\"main.svg\" alt=\"\"&#62;\n&#60;/main&#62;</code></pre></div><p>As always, I start small-screen first by adding color and typography foundation styles. This time, a light grey background, dark grey text, and a sans-serif typeface:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">body {\nbackground-color: #ededef;\nfont-family: 'sans-serif';\ncolor: #262626; }\nh1 {\ntext-align: center;\ntext-transform: uppercase; }</code></pre></div><p>The header appears first in my HTML, so I’ll style it first too by giving it a dark grey background and lighter text which is the inverse of my body styles:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">header {\nmargin-bottom: 2rem;\npadding: 2rem;\nbackground-color: #262626;\ncolor: #ededef; }</code></pre></div><figure class=\"         \"><a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d451b9ba-63ec-4293-9e22-4eb3f004fcb2/issue-12-26-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"><img srcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d451b9ba-63ec-4293-9e22-4eb3f004fcb2/issue-12-26-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d451b9ba-63ec-4293-9e22-4eb3f004fcb2/issue-12-26-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d451b9ba-63ec-4293-9e22-4eb3f004fcb2/issue-12-26-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d451b9ba-63ec-4293-9e22-4eb3f004fcb2/issue-12-26-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d451b9ba-63ec-4293-9e22-4eb3f004fcb2/issue-12-26-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\" src=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d451b9ba-63ec-4293-9e22-4eb3f004fcb2/issue-12-26-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\" sizes=\"100vw\" alt=\"This header has a dark grey background and lighter text which is the inverse of my body styles.\"/></a><figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\nThis header has a dark grey background and lighter text which is the inverse of my body styles. (<a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d451b9ba-63ec-4293-9e22-4eb3f004fcb2/issue-12-26-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">Large preview</a>)</figcaption></figure><p>Finally, for small screens, I centre that logo horizontally and limit its maximum width to half that of the viewport:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">#logo {\nmargin: 0 auto 2rem;\nmax-width: 50vw; }</code></pre></div><p>This design takes on more of a Thompson-inspired look with the extra space available on medium-size screens. I need to place elements in the header and main elements, so I add grid properties and four symmetrical columns to both:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">@media (min-width: 48em) {\nheader, main {\ndisplay: grid;\ngrid-template-columns: repeat(4, 1fr); }\n}</code></pre></div><p>Then, I add three explicit rows to my header. The first and last are 100px tall, while the middle row expands to fill all the space remaining:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">header {\ngrid-template-rows: 100px auto 100px; }</code></pre></div><p>Now it’s time to place those header elements into my columns and rows using line numbers. The Ford logo comes first and fits into the two centre columns. The headline is last and sits at the bottom while spanning the full width. I give both elements a higher z-index value, so they appear closest to the viewer in the stacking order:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">#logo {\ngrid-column: 2 / 4;\ngrid-row: 1;\nz-index: 2; }\nh1 {\ngrid-column: 1 / -1;\ngrid-row: 3;\nz-index: 2; }</code></pre></div><p>Then, I place the header image, so it covers every column and all the rows. By giving it a lower z-index value, I ensure it recedes to the bottom of the stacking order:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">header img {\ngrid-column: 1 / -1;\ngrid-row: 1 / 4;\nz-index: 1;\nalign-self: center; }</code></pre></div><p>With styles for the header image in place, I add a selector which applies those exact same styles to the image in my main element:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">header img, main img {\ngrid-column: 1 / -1;\ngrid-row: 1 / 4;\nz-index: 1;\nalign-self: center; }</code></pre></div><p>While vertical text won’t suit every design, it can turn a short passage into a strong visual statement. I change the paragraph’s writing-mode to vertical-rl and increase its leading using viewport-based units:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">main p {\nline-height: 3vw;\nwhite-space: pre-wrap;\nwriting-mode: vertical-rl; }</code></pre></div><p>For a decorative finishing touch, I change its color and apply a blending mode with a value of difference which also increases the legibility of this text where it appears over the graphic background:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">main p {\ncolor: #f4eBd5;\nmix-blend-mode: difference; }</code></pre></div><figure class=\"         \"><a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d13ccc94-5045-4bde-8751-69373ab8d652/issue-12-27-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"><img srcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d13ccc94-5045-4bde-8751-69373ab8d652/issue-12-27-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 400w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d13ccc94-5045-4bde-8751-69373ab8d652/issue-12-27-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1200/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d13ccc94-5045-4bde-8751-69373ab8d652/issue-12-27-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1200w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_1600/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d13ccc94-5045-4bde-8751-69373ab8d652/issue-12-27-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 1600w,            https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_2000/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d13ccc94-5045-4bde-8751-69373ab8d652/issue-12-27-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 2000w\" src=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d13ccc94-5045-4bde-8751-69373ab8d652/issue-12-27-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\" sizes=\"100vw\" alt=\"If you want a framework-based design to be more interesting, start by streamlining twelve narrow columns into eight wider ones.\"/></a><figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\nIf you want a framework-based design to be more interesting, start by streamlining twelve narrow columns into eight wider ones. (<a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/d13ccc94-5045-4bde-8751-69373ab8d652/issue-12-27-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">Large preview</a>)</figcaption></figure><p>I place the paragraph into the two centre columns, align it centrally, then add a higher z-index value to ensure it appears at the top of this element’s stacking order:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">main p {\ngrid-column: 2 / 4;\ngrid-row: 1 / 4;\nalign-self: center;\nz-index: 2; }</code></pre></div><figure class=\"         \"><a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2c3c72cb-2a62-4231-ad46-635d56efbec5/issue-12-28-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\"><img srcset=\"https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_400/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2c3c72cb-2a62-4231-ad46-635d56efbec5/issue-12-28-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png https://res.cloudinary.com/indysigner/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto/w_800/https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2c3c72cb-2a62-4231-ad46-635d56efbec5/issue-12-28-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png 800w, sizes=\"100vw\" alt=\"This grid is flexible and can accommodate various content types while remaining distinctive and interesting.\"/></a><figcaption class=\"op-vertical-bottom\">\nThis grid is flexible and can accommodate various content types while remaining distinctive and interesting. (<a href=\"https://cloud.netlifyusercontent.com/assets/344dbf88-fdf9-42bb-adb4-46f01eedd629/2c3c72cb-2a62-4231-ad46-635d56efbec5/issue-12-28-inspired-design-decisions-bradbury-thompson.png\">Large preview</a>)</figcaption></figure><p>Until now, this main content comes after my header in the document flow. For larger screens, I want those elements to sit side-by-side, so I apply grid properties and two symmetrical columns to the body:</p><div class=\"break-out\"><pre><code class=\"language-css\">@media (min-width: 64em) {\nbody {\ndisplay: grid;\ngrid-template-columns: 1fr 1fr;\nmin-height: 100vh; }\n}</code></pre></div><h3 id=\"staying-inspired\">Staying Inspired</h3><p>When I set out to produce this series, I wanted to teach people about the importance of for inspiration outside the web. My aim was to demonstrate that looking at the challenges designers from other media have faced &#8212; and how they approached solving them &#8212; can help us make more distinctive, engaging, and ultimately successful products and websites.</p><p>Of course, this series barely scratches the surface, and you can find inspiring examples in plenty more places than I’ve described here. Take a trip to your nearest art gallery, bookstore, museum, or record shop, and you’ll find yourself surrounded by inputs and inspiration.</p><p>I hope this series has inspired you to think about how you design for the web differently. Are examples of design from other media and periods in history relevant to the modern web? Of course, they are. Can we learn from the past while inventing the future? Absolutely. Do we have the technologies and tools to deliver more inspired designs for the web? There’s no doubt about that.</p><p>I’ve been pleased the response to this series has been overwhelmingly positive, but I know there’s plenty more I can do. This series might be coming to a close, but work has started on a new book, Inspired Design for the Web. This book will begin where Art Direction for the Web ended, will showcase more examples of inspired design, and go deeper into how we can learn lessons and apply them to make our websites and products even better.</p><h4 id=\"read-more-from-the-series\">Read More From The Series</h4><ol><li><a href=\"https://www.smashingmagazine.com/2019/06/inspired-design-decisions-avaunt-magazine/\">Inspired
